Justification for Ta'wil of Early Scholars' Statements
Sanusi justifies interpreting early scholars' statements that appear to affirm kufr as dialectical tactics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why early scholars' apparent statements of kufr should be interpreted as dialectical arguments in debates with innovators.

Core Idea
Early scholars' apparent kufr statements were dialectical weapons, not their actual beliefs.

Sanusi addresses a critical methodological issue: how to handle statements from early scholars that appear to affirm kufr. Rather than taking them literally, we must understand them as dialectical moves in debates with innovators. This lesson explains the necessity of ta'wil in such cases and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read its literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the flow from stating the problem to providing the interpretive solution.
2
Identify the core claim
Sanusi claims that it is obligatory to interpret (ta'wil) statements that seem to affirm kufr. Identify what he says should be interpreted and why.
He explicitly mentions 'the kufr of those who attribute invention to other than Allah' and 'consensus on kufr of whoever does not affirm the generality of attributes'.
3
Understand the dialectical context
The interpretation is that the early scholars spoke 'by way of dialectic' (jadaliyyan) in debating innovators. Reflect on why dialectical statements are not creedal declarations.
The purpose was to force innovators into absurd consequences of their own corrupt principles.
4
Apply the lesson
Consider how this principle affects reading other historical statements. Not everything that looks like a creedal statement is one.
This prevents misinterpretation of Islamic scholarly heritage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كُفْرِ مَنْ نسب الاختراع لغير الله تعالى، ونقل أيضاً إجماع الأمة على كفرِ مَنْ لم يقل بعموم صفاتِ الباري تبارك وتعالى. ويجب تأويلُ ما صدر عنهم إن صح النقلُ بِهِ أَنَّهُ إِنَّما قالوه على سبيلِ الجدل في مناظرة الخصومِ مِنَ المبتدعة، وإلزامهم على مقتضى أصولهم الفاسدة أقوالاً فاسدة لم يقولوا بها؛ ليُظْهِرُوا لهم أنَّهم لم يبنوا فيما يقولونَ على أساس صحيح، وإنَّما يبنون أقوالهم على أساس فاسد، فمهما بَنَوا عليه قولاً رمته رياح الجدل، وألزمتهم أنْ يُجدِّدوا على ذلك الأساس الفاسدِ بناءً آخرَ فاسداً لا ثبات له، ويوافقون على عدم استقرارِهِ، للكنْ أُلزموا أنْ يبنوه لاقتضاء أساسِهمُ الفاسدِ إِيَّاهُ، وهذا ظاهر، وبالله تعالى التوفيق.
The kufr of those who attribute invention to other than Allah, and he also transmitted the consensus of the ummah on the kufr of whoever does not affirm the generality of the attributes of al-Bari (Exalted is He). And it is necessary to interpret (ta'wil) what issued from them, if transmission of it is authentic, [to the effect] that they only said it by way of dialectic in debating the opponents among the innovators, and obligating them according to the requirements of their corrupt principles [with] corrupt statements they themselves did not hold; in order to show them that they were not building what they say upon a sound foundation, but rather build their statements upon a corrupt foundation, so whatever statement they build upon it is tossed by the winds of dialectic, and they are compelled to rebuild upon that corrupt foundation another corrupt building having no stability, and they agree upon its instability, but they are compelled to build it because their corrupt foundation requires it. And this is apparent. And by Allah is success.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage explains the justification for interpreting (ta'wil) the statements of early scholars that apparently affirm kufr. Sanusi states that it is obligatory to interpret such statements when the transmission is sound, by understanding that they were made dialectically (jadaliyyan) in debates with innovators, to show the logical consequences of the innovators' own principles. The early scholars did not actually hold those statements as their own belief. This shows that the apparent kufr statements were not meant as dogmatic assertions but as ad hominem arguments. So we should not take them literally.

Key Terms
تأويل
جدل
مبتدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Early scholars who made statements appearing to affirm kufr actually held those beliefs.
Correction: Sanusi explains that such statements were made dialectically in debates to show the logical consequences of the innovators' own principles, not as affirmations of their own creed.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why did some early scholars make statements that appear to attribute invention to other than Allah?
A) They were mistaken.
B) They were speaking dialectically against innovators.
C) They were not careful.
D) They held heretical beliefs.

Key Takeaway
Apparent kufr statements from early scholars were dialectical tactics to refute innovators, not their actual beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever stumbled upon a shocking statement from a respected scholar and immediately assumed the worst? What would it cost you to pause and investigate the context and intent behind it, as Sanusi teaches us to do?
?
In your own arguments, are you always honest about what you truly believe? Or do you sometimes say things you don't mean just to win a debate, like the early scholars did? If so, how can you reconcile that with the command to be truthful in all matters?

Imam al-Razi's Debate with a Christian Scholar
Al-Razi narrates his encounter with a Christian scholar and his method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Razi's method of first establishing rational ground before debating theological opponents.

Core Idea
Before debating, teach your opponent a rational principle.

This short passage captures a key moment in Imam al-Razi's intellectual biography. Instead of charging into argument, al-Razi first taught his opponent a single rational principle. The lesson is not about the principle itself, but about the methodological insight: correct reasoning must begin on shared rational foundations.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the setting: a debate between al-Razi and a Christian scholar.
The passage is short but dense with meaning.
2
Observe al-Razi's diagnosis
Al-Razi found his opponent 'extremely far from rationality.' What does this imply about the opponent's approach?
Al-Razi sees a lack of rational method, not just wrong conclusions.
3
Identify the one principle
Al-Razi taught him a single principle. The principle itself is not revealed, but the focus is on the act of teaching before debating.
Why only one principle? Because a single foundational rule can transform a debate.
4
Reflect on the method
Consider why establishing a rational principle first is essential. How does this method prevent aimless argument?
This anecdote illustrates a pedagogical tactic still relevant today.

This highlights the importance of establishing agreed-upon rational grounds before engaging in theological argumentation. The passage shows al-Razi's method: first correct the foundational methodology, then proceed with the debate. The specific principle is not mentioned here, but the emphasis is on the approach.

?

?
Al-Razi, a great scholar, took time to teach a single principle. Are you impatient when explaining Islam? Do you expect immediate agreement without laying the groundwork? Commit today to preparing one clear, rational premise before your next discussion about your faith.

The Reductio Refutation of Skepticism
Sanusi refutes a skeptic by turning his own principle against him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses a reductio ad absurdum argument to refute a skeptic who denies the possibility of multiple gods, exposing the logical inconsistency in the skeptic's own principle.

Core Idea
If absence of evidence doesn't prove absence, then everything is possible – even beetles as gods.

Sanusi presents a powerful logical attack on a skeptic who claims that there is no evidence for multiple gods. By using the skeptic's own admission that absence of evidence is not proof of absence, Sanusi forces the skeptic into an absurd conclusion. This lesson walks through the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the argument's flow become clear before diving into commentary.
Notice the Quranic verse at the end – it confirms the outcome.
2
Identify the skeptic's principle
Sanusi refers to the skeptic's claim that 'absence of evidence does not necessitate absence of the thing evidenced.' Identify this as the key principle the skeptic holds.
3
Follow the reductio
Sanusi proposes a test: could contemptible animals like beetles be gods? The skeptic says no, due to lack of evidence. But Sanusi points out that by the skeptic's own principle, lack of evidence does not disprove beetle-gods. This creates a contradiction.
The absurd conclusion is that beetles might be gods – something the skeptic must reject.
4
Reflect on the Quranic ending
The verse 'Then the disbeliever was confounded' shows the skeptic is left speechless. Consider how this argument silences the skeptic without needing further evidence.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum – reducing an opponent's position to an absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قلتُ له (۱) : هل يجوز أن نكون نحن وهذه الحيوانات المحتقره كالخنافس ونحوها آلهة ؟ فقال : لا أُجوِّزَ ذلكَ ؛ لعدم دليل الألوهية فيها فقلتُ له : كيف وقد سلَّمْتَ أنَّهُ لا يلزمُ مِنْ عدمِ الدليل عدم المدلول ؟! فلعلها تكونُ آلهةً في نفس الأمر على مقتضى أصلكم ولم يظهر لكم بعد دليلُ أُلوهِيَّتِها ؟! ﴿ فَبُهِتَ الَّذِي كَفَرَ وَاللَّهُ لَا يَهْدِى الْقَوْمَ الظَّالِمِينَ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٥٨] (٢)
Then I said to him: 'Is it permissible that we and these contemptible animals, like beetles and the like, be gods?' He said: 'I do not allow that, due to the absence of evidence of divinity in them.' So I said to him: 'How (can you say that) when you have conceded that absence of evidence does not necessitate absence of the thing evidenced? Perhaps they are gods in reality according to your principle, and the evidence of their divinity has not yet appeared to you?' Then the disbeliever was confounded. And Allah does not guide the wrongdoing people. (Quran 2:258)
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents a reductio ad absurdum argument against a skeptic who denies the possibility of multiple gods. The author first asks whether lowly creatures like beetles could be gods. The skeptic refuses because there is no evidence of divinity in them. The author then points out that the skeptic's own principle—that absence of evidence does not prove absence—would allow such a possibility. Thus, the skeptic is forced either to accept that beetles might be gods (absurd) or to abandon his principle. The Quranic verse confirms his bafflement.

Key Terms
الإلهية
الدليل
المدلول
البهت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That absence of evidence is sufficient to disprove a claim.
Correction: The passage shows that absence of evidence does not prove absence; a claim can only be disproven by positive evidence or logical contradiction.

Checkpoint
What logical flaw does Sanusi expose in the skeptic's response?
A) The skeptic denies evidence without examining it.
B) The skeptic uses a double standard: he requires evidence for insect gods but not for his own position.
C) The skeptic concedes that absence of evidence does not prove absence, yet he uses absence of evidence to deny insect gods.
D) The skeptic fails to provide a definition of divinity.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's reductio argument shows that a principle allowing anything in the absence of evidence leads to absurdities, thereby refuting the skeptic's position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you accepted a principle without considering where it leads? What absurdities might you be tolerating in your own beliefs right now?
?
Are there beliefs you hold simply because you have no evidence against them? Is that a valid reason? Would you be comfortable applying that logic to other areas of your life?
?
The skeptic was confounded when his own reasoning was turned against him. Where in your life might your own arguments be turned against you if you are not consistent? What will you do about that?

The Necessity of Prophets for Divine Knowledge
Sanusi concludes that intellects cannot know divine rulings, so prophets are necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human reason alone cannot know Allah's legal rulings and why prophets are necessary.

Core Idea
Reason cannot know divine law; only revelation through prophets provides certainty.

After establishing Allah's absolute sovereignty, Sanusi now draws a crucial conclusion: human intellects are inherently limited when it comes to knowing Allah's commands and prohibitions. This passage explains why analogical reasoning fails and why we need prophets who are truthful and protected from error. Let's read the passage carefully to see the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation once to grasp the overall argument. Notice the opening phrase 'فيلزم من هذا كله' which signals a conclusion from prior premises.
2
Identify the conclusion
The passage states that intellects are incapable (عجز العقول) of perceiving divine rulings. Find the reason given: there is no likeness to Allah for analogical reasoning.
3
Understand the reason
Why does analogy fail? Because nothing is comparable to Allah—neither present (شاهد) nor absent (غائب). This blocks any attempt to derive rulings by human reason alone.
4
Recognize the necessity of prophets
Knowledge of reward, punishment, permissible, etc. comes only from Allah through His messengers. Note the three key features: they are sent, supported by proofs of truthfulness, and protected from sin.
5
Reflect on the doctrine
Ask yourself: Why is the protection (عصمة) of prophets emphasized? How does this passage refute those who think reason suffices for moral knowledge?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيلزمُ مِنْ هذا كلّهِ عجز العقول عن إدراك أحكامه الشرعيَّةِ مِنْ جهة فكرتها وقياساتها ؛ إذ لا مثلَ له تبارك وتعالى لا شاهداً ولا غائباً يُقاس عليهِ ، وإنَّما تُدرَكُ أمارةُ الثواب والعقاب ، وما يُباحُ وما لا يُباحُ ، وحقائق ذلك وكيفياتُهُ وأوقاتُهُ . . من جهة المولى العظيم ؛ بمَنْ بعثَهُ مِنْ رُسُلِهِ الكرام ، الذينَ أَيَّدَهم بأدلَّةِ صِدْقِهم في كلّ ما يُبلغونَ عنه ، وعصمهم بفضلِهِ في جميع أقوالهم وأفعالهم واعتقاداتهم مِنْ كلَّ ما ينهى سبحانَهُ عنه نهي تحريم أو كراهة .
So it follows from all of this the incapacity of intellects to perceive His legal rulings by means of their thought and analogies, for there is no likeness to Him, Blessed and Exalted is He, neither present nor absent, that could be compared to Him. Rather, the indication of reward and punishment, and what is permissible and what is not permissible, and the realities of that, its modalities, and its times, are known only from the Mighty Lord, through whom He sent from among His noble messengers, whom He supported with proofs of their truthfulness in everything they convey from Him, and He protected them by His grace in all their statements, actions, and beliefs from everything that He, Exalted is He, forbids them, whether by prohibition of prohibition or dislike.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion and an argument for the necessity of prophethood. It states that from all the previous points (Allah's absolute sovereignty, His direct creation, etc.) it necessarily follows that human intellects are incapable of independently perceiving Allah's legal rulings (ahkam shari'iyyah) through their own thought and analogies (qiyasat). The reason is that nothing is comparable to Allah—neither something present in this world nor something absent—so analogical reasoning cannot apply. Therefore, knowledge of what constitutes reward, punishment, permissible, forbidden, their realities, modalities, and times comes only from Allah through His messengers. These messengers are supported by proofs of their truthfulness (adillat sidq) in everything they convey. Additionally, Allah protects them (isma) by His grace in all their statements, actions, and beliefs from anything He forbids, whether as a prohibition of prohibition (tahrim) or of dislike (karaha). This establishes the foundational Sunni doctrine that reason alone is insufficient for moral and legal knowledge; divine revelation is essential.

Key Terms

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human reason can independently know moral and legal truths without revelation.
Correction: This passage states that intellects are incapable of perceiving divine legal rulings through thought and analogy because there is no likeness to Allah; such knowledge comes only from Allah through His messengers.

Checkpoint
Why are intellects incapable of knowing Allah's legal rulings according to this passage?
A) Because rulings are too difficult.
B) Because there is no likeness to Allah that can be used for analogy.
C) Because Allah hides them.
D) Because intellects are inherently flawed.

Key Takeaway
Human intellects cannot know Allah's legal rulings through analogy; only revelation from prophets, who are supported by proofs and protected from error, provides that knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you believe that prophets are the only source of divine knowledge, are you actively seeking that knowledge from the Quran and Sunnah, or do you trust your own opinions? What one step can you take today to prioritize revelation over your own reasoning in a specific area of your life?

No Excuse for Ignorance After Clear Proofs
Sanusi cites al-Ghazali on inexcusability after decisive proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why ignorance of fundamental religious beliefs is not excused once clear proofs have been provided by God.

Core Idea
Clear proofs remove the excuse for ignorance.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle from Imam al-Ghazali that underlies the obligation to reflect on the fundamentals of faith. The source passage, quoted by Sanusi, asserts that God's decisive proofs leave no room for excuse, and that these proofs are made accessible to all. This lesson unpacks that claim and its implications for every rational person.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic text aloud if possible, then the English translation. Notice the structure: a general statement, a quote from al-Ghazali, and then an elaboration from Sanusi's commentary.
The passage uses a chain of citations: Sanusi quotes al-Ghazali, then the author of Sharh Kifayat al-Murid.
2
Identify al-Ghazali's golden words
Find the phrase attributed to al-Ghazali: 'There is no excuse with God's setting up of decisive proofs.' Ask yourself: what does this mean for someone who claims ignorance?
This is the core principle. It shifts responsibility onto the learner.
3
Understand the commentary's expansion
Read the commentary from Sharh Kifayat al-Murid. It explains that all proofs of tawhid are clearly presented in the Qur'an and Sunnah, understandable by everyone regardless of intelligence. Why does this strengthen the argument?
The commentary emphasizes the accessibility and multiplicity of proofs.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that there is no excuse for abandoning obligatory reflection (nazar) because it is easy for every rational person. Consider what this implies about the duty to seek knowledge of tawhid.
This connects the principle to action: one must engage in reasoned reflection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) وما كلف الله تعالى به عباده من أصول الدين والمعرفة . . لا يعذرون بالجهل به ؛ حتى قال حجة الإسلام كلمته الذهبية في ذلك في « المستصفى » : ( لا عذر مع نصب الله تعالى الأدلة القاطعة ) ، ولذا قال المصنف في « شرح كفاية المريد » وهو « شرح الجزائرية » ( ص ٥١ ) : ( وما من دليل من أدلة عقائد التوحيد إلا وهو مقول مبيَّن في الكتاب والسنة بأوجه من البيان متكاثرة ؛ بحيث يستوي في فهمها الغبي والذكي ، والقوي والضعيف فلا عذر إذاً في ترك النظر الواجب ؛ لسهولته على كل عاقل أعظم سهولة )
(1) And what God Almighty has obligated upon His servants of the fundamentals of religion and knowledge... they are not excused by ignorance of it; until the Proof of Islam said his golden words about that in al-Mustasfa: 'There is no excuse with God's setting up of decisive proofs.' Therefore, the author said in 'Sharh Kifayat al-Murid,' which is 'Sharh al-Jaza'iriyya' (p. 51): 'There is not a single proof from the proofs of the doctrines of tawhid except that it is expressed and clarified in the Book and the Sunnah with multiple aspects of clarification, such that the dull-witted and the intelligent, the strong and the weak, are equal in understanding it. So there is no excuse therefore for abandoning the obligatory reflection, due to its being of the greatest ease for every rational person.'
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a supporting citation from a footnote. It quotes Imam al-Ghazali's principle from al-Mustasfa: human beings are not excused by ignorance because God has provided decisive proofs. Then the author (Sanusi or the commentator) adds that every proof of tawhid is clearly expressed in the Qur'an and Sunnah in multiple ways, accessible to all intellects, so there is no excuse for neglecting the obligatory reflection (nazar) due to its ease.

نظر واجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A person is excused for ignorance of religious fundamentals if they have not studied them formally.
Correction: No, because God has provided clear and accessible proofs in the Qur'an and Sunnah; therefore, ignorance is not an excuse.

Checkpoint
According to the citation from al-Ghazali, what removes the excuse for ignorance?
A) The existence of the Qur'an and Sunnah alone.
B) God's setting up of decisive proofs.
C) The obligation of reflection.
D) The ease of understanding.

Key Takeaway
God's decisive proofs remove any excuse for ignorance about fundamental beliefs, making obligatory reflection incumbent upon every rational person.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
You now know that Allah has set up decisive proofs that remove all excuses. If you were to stand before Him tomorrow and He asked why you did not seek knowledge of Him, would your excuse hold? What one concrete step will you take this week to engage with those proofs?
?
The author says that every proof of tawhid is expressed in the Quran and Sunnah in ways that both the strong and weak can grasp. Are you relying on scholars alone instead of reflecting yourself? How will you personally take ownership of your belief starting today?

The Third Matter: Bad Imitation and Its Consequences
Sanusi defines bad imitation and categorizes its outcomes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what Sanusi means by bad imitation and how it can lead either to clear disbelief (kufr) or to disputed innovation (bid'ah).

Core Idea
Bad imitation is not equal—it can lead to kufr or bid'ah.

Sanusi continues his enumeration of essential theological matters. Here he addresses the third matter: the invalidity of bad imitation. This is not a blanket condemnation of all imitation, but a careful distinction between imitation that results in unambiguous disbelief and imitation that results in doctrinal innovation whose severity is debated. The passage provides concrete historical examples to ground this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Let Sanusi's own words present the distinction first.
Notice the two categories of consequences.
2
Identify the two consequences
The passage lists two outcomes of bad imitation: explicit kufr (with examples) and disputed bid'ah. Mark each in the text.
3
Reflect on the examples
Sanusi gives examples for each category. Ask yourself why these are considered bad imitation and how they differ in ruling.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأمرُ الثالث بطلان التقليد الرديء؛ وهو التقليد الردي: فقد نشأ عنه كفر صريحٌ مُجمَعٌ عليهِ؛ وهو تقليدُ الجاهليَّةِ آباءهم في الشركِ وعبادة الأصنام، وتقليد عامَّةِ اليهود وعامة النصارى لأحبارهم في إنكار نبوَّةِ نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ، ونحو ذلكَ مِنْ كلٌّ تقليد في كفر صريح ونشأ عنه بدعةٌ مُختلفٌ في كفر صاحبها: كتقليد عامة المعتزلة والمرجئة والمجسمة لقدمائهم فيما دانوا بهِ مِنْ هذهِ البِدَعِ، وقد سبق في ذلكَ مِنَ الخلافِ.
As for the third matter: the invalidity of bad imitation; it is bad imitation: for it has resulted in explicit kufr upon which there is consensus; namely, the imitation by the Jahiliyyah of their fathers in shirk and worship of idols, and the imitation by the common Jews and common Christians of their rabbis in denying the prophethood of our Prophet and our Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and similar imitations that are explicit kufr. And it has resulted in bid'ah concerning which there is disagreement regarding the kufr of its perpetrator: such as the imitation by the common Mu'tazila, Murji'a, and Mujassima of their predecessors in the bid'ah they professed. And there has already preceded discussion of this difference of opinion.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage defines the third matter (al-amr al-thalith) mentioned by Sanusi, which is the invalidity of bad imitation (bāṭil al-taqlīd al-radī'). Bad imitation is defined as following someone in error without proof. Sanusi then categorizes its consequences into two types: (1) clear kufr on which there is unanimous agreement among Muslims. Examples include the pre-Islamic Arabs imitating their ancestors in polytheism and idol worship, and common Jews and Christians imitating their religious leaders in denying the prophethood of Muhammad ﷺ. (2) Bid'ah (innovation) about which scholars differ as to whether it constitutes kufr. Examples include the common followers of the Mu'tazila, Murji'a, and Mujassima who blindly follow their sectarian leaders in their innovated beliefs. Sanusi notes that this difference of opinion among scholars has been previously mentioned (referring to earlier discussion). The passage establishes that not all imitation is blameworthy; it is the object of imitation that determines the ruling.

Key Terms
الامر الثالث
التقليد الرديء
كفر صريح
بدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All imitation is equally blameworthy.
Correction: Sanusi teaches that bad imitation specifically leads to kufr or bid'ah, but praiseworthy imitation (following proof) is not condemned.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does bad imitation (al-taqlīd al-radī') lead to?
A) Only bid'ah without kufr
B) Either explicit kufr on which there is consensus, or bid'ah concerning which kufr is disputed
C) Always explicit kufr
D) Only minor sin

Key Takeaway
Bad imitation leads either to clear kufr (consensus) or to bid'ah (disputed kufr), depending on what is being followed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there beliefs or practices in your life that you have simply inherited from your family or culture without ever questioning them against revelation? What would it cost you to examine them today?
?
When you follow a scholar or a group, do you do so because you have verified their evidence, or because it feels safe? How would you respond if someone asked you, 'Why do you believe that?' and you could not quote a single verse or hadith?
?
This passage shows that blind imitation can lead to kufr or bid'ah. If you discovered tomorrow that something you believe is actually a bid'ah, would you have the courage to abandon it even if it meant losing the approval of those around you?

Good Imitation and the Four Madhhabs
Sanusi distinguishes good imitation from bad and affirms following the four madhhabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between good and bad imitation in Islamic jurisprudence and why following the four madhhabs is considered following the saved majority.

Core Idea
Following the four madhhabs is not blind imitation but following the saved majority.

Sanusi now addresses a practical concern: how should ordinary Muslims approach matters of fiqh? He distinguishes between two types of imitation and identifies the only valid schools to follow today. This passage grounds the practice of taqlid in prophetic command and scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Sanusi defines good imitation and then lists the four imams.
2
Understand the distinction
Sanusi distinguishes 'good imitation' (taqlid hasan) from 'bad imitation' (taqlid radī'). Good imitation is following scholars in subsidiary matters. Identify what makes it good.
Bad imitation might be following in matters that require ijtihad or following without authority.
3
Identify the four madhhabs
Sanusi names the four imams: Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmed. He says their followers today represent the 'sawad al-muslimin' (majority). Note this term.
This is a key concept: the great majority.
4
Examine the supporting quotes
Sanusi quotes al-Dehlawi, al-Sawi, and al-Baghdadi. Each provides a different angle: hadith, prohibition, and creedal affiliation.
Notice the strong warning from al-Sawi.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends by acknowledging that taqlid is not perfect, but it is a legitimate guidance. Consider why Sanusi includes this concession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حُسْنُ تقليد العلماء المجتهدين في الفروع. واحترزَ بـ ( التقليدِ الرديءِ ) مِنَ التقليد الحسنِ؛ كتقليد عامَّةِ المؤمنينَ لعلمائهم في الفروع. والفقهاء اليوم الذين يجوز تقليدهم، والتمذهب بمذاهبهم.. هم أعلام المذاهب الأربعة المتبوعة؛ أبو حنيفة ومالك والشافعي وأحمد، رضي عنهم أجمعين، وأتباعهم اليوم من يمثل سواد المسلمين. قال العلامة الدهلوي في « عقد الجيد في أحكام الاجتهاد والتقليد » ( ص ١٣ ) : ( قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «اتبعوا السواد الأعظم » ، ولما اندرست المذاهب الحقة إلا هذه الأربعة .. كان اتباعها اتباعاً للسواد الأعظم والخروج عنها خروجاً عن السواد الأعظم ). وقال العلامة الصاوي في حاشيته على الجلالين ) ( ٢/ ٣٦٤ ) : ( ولا يجوز تقليد ما عدا المذاهب الأربعة ، ولو وافق قول الصحابة والحديث الصحيح والآية ، فالخارج عن المذاهب الأربعة ضال مضل ). وقال الإمام عبد القاهر البغدادي في «الفرق بين الفرق » ( ص ٢٦٧ ) : ( والصنف الثاني من أهل السنة والجماعة : أئمة الفقه من فريقي الرأي والحديث ؛ من الذين اعتقدوا مذاهب الصفاتية في الله تعالى وفي صفاته الأزلية ، وتبرَّؤوا من القدر والاعتزال، وأثبتوا رؤية الله تعالى بالأبصار ، من غير تشبيه ولا تعطيل ، ويدخل في هذه الجماعة : أصحاب مالك والشافعي والأوزاعي والثوري وأبي حنيفة وابن أبي ليلى ، وأصحاب أبي ثور ، وأصحاب أحمد بن حنبل ، وأهل الظاهر ، وسائر الفقهاء الذين اعتقدوا في الأبواب العقدية أصول الصفاتية، ولم يخلطوا فقههم بشيء من بدع أهل الأهواء الضالة ). نعم؛ لا يكون التقليد كمالاً، ولكنَّه هداية أقرتها الشريعة.
The excellence of imitating mujtahid scholars in subsidiary matters. And he made an exception with (bad imitation) from good imitation; such as the imitation by the common believers of their scholars in subsidiary matters. And the jurists today whom it is permissible to imitate and to adopt as a madhhab are the notable figures of the four followed madhhabs: Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, may Allah be pleased with them all, and their followers today represent the mass of the Muslims. Al-Allama al-Dehlawi said in 'Iqd al-Jayyid fi Ahkam al-Ijtihad wa al-Taqlid' (p. 13): (The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Follow the great majority' and when the true madhhabs became extinct except these four, following them is following the great majority and leaving them is leaving the great majority.) And al-Allama al-Sawi said in his gloss on al-Jalalayn (2/364): (It is not permissible to imitate other than the four madhhabs, even if it agrees with the statement of a Companion or an authentic hadith or a verse; for the one who leaves the four madhhabs is misguided and misguiding.) And Imam Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi said in al-Farq bayn al-Firaq (p. 267): (The second group of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a are the imams of fiqh from both the people of opinion and the people of hadith; those who believed in the doctrines of the Sifatiyya concerning Allah and His eternal attributes, and disavowed Qadr and I'tizal, and affirmed the vision of Allah with the eyes, without tashbih or ta'til; and this group includes: the followers of Malik, al-Shafi'i, al-Awza'i, al-Thawri, Abu Hanifa, Ibn Abi Layla, the followers of Abu Thawr, the followers of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the Zahiris, and all the jurists who believed in the principles of the Sifatiyya in doctrinal matters and did not mix their fiqh with any of the innovations of the misguided people of desires.) Yes, imitation is not perfection, but it is a guidance that the Shari'a has confirmed.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage clarifies the distinction between good imitation (al-taqlīd al-ḥasan) and bad imitation (al-taqlīd al-radī'). Sanusi states that good imitation is exemplified by common Muslims following their scholars in subsidiary matters of fiqh (furūʿ). He then identifies the specific scholars who are valid to follow today: the four founders of the mainstream madhhabs - Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal (may Allah be pleased with them). Their followers constitute the vast majority of Muslims (sawād al-muslimīn). To support this, Sanusi quotes three authorities: al-Dehlawi cites the hadith 'Follow the great majority' and argues that because only these four madhhabs remain, following them is obligatory and leaving them is leaving the majority. Al-Sawi states that it is forbidden to follow any madhhab outside the four, even if it appears to agree with a Companion, authentic hadith, or verse; leaving them leads to misguidance. Al-Baghdadi includes the followers of these four imams (along with others like al-Awza'i, al-Thawri, etc.) under Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, emphasizing their adherence to the Sifatiyya creed (affirming Allah's attributes without tashbih or ta'til) and their rejection of Qadariyya, Mu'tazila, and other innovators. The passage concludes by noting that while imitation (taqlīd) is not the highest level of perfection (which is ijtihad), it is a valid guidance sanctioned by the Shari'a.

Key Terms
التقليد الحسن
المذاهب الأربعة
السواد الأعظم
الفروع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That following a madhhab is blind imitation without evidence
Correction: Rather, it is following the saved majority as commanded by the Prophet ﷺ, and is grounded in scholarly authority and consensus.

Checkpoint
According to al-Sawi, what is the ruling on following a madhhab outside the four?
A) Permissible if it agrees with a hadith
B) Not permissible; the one who leaves the four is misguided
C) Permissible but not preferred
D) Permissible only for scholars

Key Takeaway
Good imitation (taqlid hasan) means following the four madhhabs, which represent the saved majority of Muslims and is sanctioned by Sharia.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that following the four madhhabs is following the saved majority. Do you actively follow one of these madhhabs in your worship, or do you pick and choose based on convenience? What would it cost you to commit fully to one of these guided paths, and are you willing to pay that price?
?
Al-Sawi declared that leaving the four madhhabs is misguidance, even if you find a hadith that seems stronger. Is there an area of your practice where you prioritize your own reasoning over the established madhhab? Examine your heart: are you seeking truth or your own independence?
?
Imitation (taqlid) is not perfection, but it is guidance. Are you content to be among the guided majority, or do you secretly wish to be a mujtahid when you lack the qualifications? What does your attitude towards the madhhabs reveal about your humility before Allah and His scholars?

Good Taqlid vs Bad Taqlid in Furu‘
Distinguishes good taqlid from bad and discusses takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between praiseworthy taqlid (following scholars in branches of fiqh) and blameworthy taqlid, and why the former is considered good.

Core Idea
Not all taqlid is the same: following scholars in fiqh is good, blind imitation in creed is bad.

This passage begins by clarifying that the discussion is about the goodness of taqlid in branches, not about blind imitation or bad taqlid. It distinguishes between good taqlid—like that of ordinary believers following their scholars in matters of fiqh—and bad taqlid. The text also addresses a related issue about takfir, showing the careful approach of the early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening distinction
Notice how the passage immediately distinguishes good taqlid from bad taqlid by setting apart (ihtiraz) the bad kind.
The word 'ihtiraz' signals a technical exclusion.
2
Understand the qibla example
The passage gives an example of good taqlid: laypeople following scholars about the qibla direction. Note the principle: ignorance of attributes is not ignorance of the described.
This example shows that taqlid in practical matters is permissible.
3
Reflect on the takfir discussion
The passage quotes an imam that most companions refrain from takfir except in clear cases of denial.
This shows the caution of early scholars in declaring someone a disbeliever.

حُسْنُ تقليد العلماء المجتهدين في الفروع ] واحترزَ بـ ( التقليدِ الرديء ( مِنَ التقليد الحسنِ ؛ كتقليد عامَّةِ المؤمنينَ لعلمائهم في الفروع (1) القبلة ؛ لأن الجهل بالصفات ليس جهلاً بالموصوفات ، وقال : « اختلفنا عبارة والمشار إليه واحد ) إلى أن قال : ( قال الإمام : ومعظم الأصحاب على ترك التكفير ، وقالوا : إنما نكفّر من جهل وجود الرب ، أو علم وجوده ولكن الله فعل فعلاً أو قال قولاً أجمعت الأمة على أنه لا يصدر ذلك إلا عن كافر » ) (۱) والفقهاء اليوم الذين يجوز تقليدهم ، والتمذهب بمذاهبهم .. هم أعلام المذاهب الأربعة المتبوعة ؛ أبو حنيفة ومالك والشافعي وأحمد ، رضي عنهم أجمعين، وأتباعهم اليوم من يمثل سواد المسلمين ، قال العلامة الدهلوي في « عقد الجيد في أحكام الاجتهاد والتقليد » ( ص ١٣ ) : ( قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «اتبعوا السواد الأعظم » ، ولما اندرست المذاهب الحقة إلا هذه الأربعة .. كان اتباعها اتباعاً للسواد الأعظم والخروج عنها خروجاً عن السواد الأعظم ) . ، وقال العلامة الصاوي في حاشيته على الجلالين ) ( ٢/ ٣٦٤ ) : ( ولا يجوز تقليد ما عدا المذاهب الأربعة ، ولو وافق قول الصحابة والحديث الصحيح والآية ، فالخارج عن المذاهب الأربعة ضال مضل ) وقال الإمام عبد القاهر البغدادي في «الفرق بين الفرق » ( ص ٢٦٧ ) : ) والصنف الثاني من أهل السنة والجماعة : أئمة الفقه من فريقي الرأي والحديث ؛ من الذين اعتقدوا مذاهب الصفاتية في الله تعالى وفي صفاته الأزلية ، وتبرَّؤوا من القدر والاعتزال، وأثبتوا رؤية الله تعالى بالأبصار ، من غير تشبيه ولا تعطيل ، ويدخل في هذه الجماعة : أصحاب مالك والشافعي والأوزاعي والثوري وأبي حنيفة وابن أبي ليلى ، وأصحاب أبي ثور ، وأصحاب أحمد بن حنبل ، وأهل الظاهر ، وسائر الفقهاء الذين اعتقدوا في الأبواب العقدية أصول الصفاتية ، ولم يخلطوا فقههم بشيء من بدع أهل الأهواء الضالة ) ، نعم ؛ لا يكون التقليد كمالاً، ولكنَّه هداية أقرتها الشريعة
The goodness of following mujtahid scholars in branches] And he guarded against (bad following) from good following; like the following of the general believers for their scholars in branches (1) the qibla; because ignorance of the attributes is not ignorance of the described, and he said: 'We differed in expression and the referred-to is one' until he said: 'The Imam said: Most of the companions are for refraining from takfir, and they said: We only declare takfir on one who is ignorant of the existence of the Lord, or knows His existence but God did an action or said a statement that the umma has consensus that such does not issue except from a disbeliever)' (1) And the jurists today whom it is permissible to follow, and to adopt their schools... are the leaders of the four followed madhabs: Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, may God be pleased with them all, and their followers today are those who represent the masses of the Muslims. Al-‘Allama al-Dahlawi said in '‘Iqd al-Jayyid fi Ahkam al-Ijtihad wa al-Taqlid' (p. 13): 'The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said: "Follow the greater mass." And when the true schools became extinct except these four... following them is following the greater mass, and leaving them is leaving the greater mass.' And al-‘Allama al-Sawi said in his gloss on al-Jalalayn (2/364): 'It is not permissible to follow other than the four madhabs, even if it agrees with the saying of the Companions, the authentic hadith, and the verse; so whoever leaves the four madhabs is misguided and misguiding.' And Imam ‘Abd al-Qahir al-Baghdadi said in 'al-Farq bayn al-Firaq' (p. 267): 'The second category of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama‘a: the imams of fiqh from the two groups of opinion and hadith; those who believed in the schools of the Sifatiyya concerning God Almighty and His eternal attributes, and disassociated from Qadr and I‘tizal, and affirmed the vision of God with eyes, without tashbih or ta‘til. And included in this group are: the followers of Malik, al-Shafi‘i, al-Awza‘i, al-Thawri, Abu Hanifa, Ibn Abi Layla, the followers of Abu Thawr, the followers of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the Zahiris, and the rest of the jurists who believed in the principles of the Sifatiyya in creedal matters, and did not mix their fiqh with any of the innovations of the people of misguided desires.' Yes; following is not perfection, but it is guidance that the Shari‘a has approved.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage defines and defends the goodness (husn) of following (taqlid) mujtahid scholars in the branches of fiqh (furu‘). It begins by distinguishing bad taqlid from good: bad taqlid is excluded, while good taqlid is exemplified by the general believers following their scholars in furu‘. A quotation clarifies that ignorance of attributes is not ignorance of the described, and that most companions avoid takfir except for clear deniers. The passage then states that today the permissible scholars to follow are the four madhabs, and their followers represent the Muslim masses. Support is provided by al-Dahlawi, who cites the hadith 'Follow the greater mass' and notes that only these four madhabs remain, so following them is following the greater mass. Al-Sawi asserts that leaving these four is misguidance. Al-Baghdadi includes the imams of these madhabs in the second category of Ahl al-Sunna, praising their creedal orthodoxy. The passage concludes by affirming that taqlid is not perfection but is a guidance approved by the Shari‘a.

Key Terms
تقليد
فروع
تكفير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All taqlid is blameworthy and should be avoided.
Correction: The passage distinguishes between good taqlid (following scholars in branches) and bad taqlid. Good taqlid is praised and exemplified by the practice of ordinary believers.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what kind of taqlid is considered good?
A) Following scholars in matters of creed
B) Following scholars in branches like qibla direction
C) Blindly imitating any opinion
D) Rejecting all scholarship

Key Takeaway
Good taqlid in branches of fiqh is commendable and distinct from blameworthy blind imitation in creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you follow a scholar in a fiqh ruling, do you do so with the awareness that you are performing good taqlid, or have you ever fallen into blind imitation without seeking the evidence? How can you make your taqlid in furu‘ more conscious and accountable to the truth?
?
Have you ever judged someone’s faith based on a theological disagreement you did not fully understand? This lesson teaches extreme caution in takfir. Examine your heart: is there anyone you have considered less of a Muslim due to differences in creed? What will you do to rectify that?
?
The companions refrained from takfir even over attribute differences, because they distinguished between ignorance of attributes and ignorance of God. Do you have the same restraint, or are you quick to label others? What specific step can you take today to guard your tongue from careless judgments?

The Four Madhabs and the Greater Mass
Affirms the four madhabs as the only ones to follow today.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why following the four Sunni madhabs is obligatory and how they represent the 'greater mass' (al-sawad al-a‘zam) of Muslims.

Core Idea
The four madhabs are the only surviving true schools; following them is following the Muslim majority.

After establishing the goodness of taqlid in general, the passage now specifies which scholars are permissible to follow today: the four madhabs. It cites two authorities—al-Dahlawi and al-Sawi—to affirm that these schools represent the 'greater mass' and that leaving them is misguidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four madhabs
The passage names the four imams: Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi‘i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Note that their followers today represent the Muslim masses.
These are the only ones considered permissible to follow.
2
Understand al-Dahlawi's argument
He quotes the hadith 'Follow the greater mass' and explains that since only these four true schools remain, following them is following the greater mass.
This links taqlid with communal solidarity.
3
Analyze al-Sawi's ruling
Al-Sawi states that it is not permissible to follow any other school, even if it agrees with a sahih hadith or a Companion's saying. Leaving the four is being misguided and misguiding.
This is a strong statement on the exclusivity of the four madhabs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is permissible to follow any scholar or school as long as their opinion is supported by evidence.
Correction: Al-Sawi explicitly states that even if an opinion agrees with a verse, hadith, or Companion's saying, it is not permissible to follow a school outside the four madhabs.

Checkpoint
What does al-Sawi say about following a school other than the four madhabs?
A) It is permissible if it matches a sahih hadith.
B) It is not permissible, and doing so makes one misguided.
C) It is recommended.
D) It is only discouraged.

Key Takeaway
The four madhabs are the only surviving true schools, and following them is obligatory as they represent the greater mass of Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever chosen an opinion from outside the four madhabs because it seemed easier or more appealing? How does the warning of being 'misguided and misguiding' weigh on your conscience? What step will you take to align with the greater mass?
?
The hadith says 'Follow the greater mass.' In your daily practice, do you genuinely seek out the teachings of the four madhabs, or do you follow what is popular or convenient? What does your choice say about your commitment to the Prophet's command?
?
Al-Sawi states that even if an opinion agrees with a sahih hadith, leaving the four madhabs is still forbidden. Does this confront your assumption that following the evidence directly is always better? How does this teaching challenge your personal approach to seeking religious knowledge?

The Scholars of Ahl al-Sunna and the Value of Taqlid
Classifies scholars and concludes on taqlid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the imams of the four madhabs are included in Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama‘a and why taqlid, though not perfection, is a divinely approved guidance.

Core Idea
The four madhabs belong to Ahl al-Sunna, and taqlid is a valid, recognized guidance.

The passage concludes by placing the four madhabs within the broader category of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama‘a. Al-Baghdadi's classification includes not only the four but also other early jurists who adhered to orthodox creed. Finally, the author affirms that taqlid is not the highest level of perfection but is a guidance approved by Shari‘a.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Baghdadi's classification
Al-Baghdadi describes the second category of Ahl al-Sunna: the jurists of the two groups (people of opinion and hadith) who followed the Sifatiyya creed. Note the list of included scholars.
The list includes more than just the four, showing the broad orthodox consensus.
2
Identify the creedal conditions
These jurists believed in God's eternal attributes, rejected Qadr and I‘tizal, affirmed seeing God, and avoided tashbih and ta‘til.
This shows the link between fiqh and correct theology.
3
Understand the final statement
The passage ends: 'Yes; taqlid is not perfection, but it is guidance that the Shari‘a has approved.' This tempers the earlier strong affirmations.
Taqlid is a concession, not the ideal.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حُسْنُ تقليد العلماء المجتهدين في الفروع ] واحترزَ بـ ( التقليدِ الرديء ( مِنَ التقليد الحسنِ ؛ كتقليد عامَّةِ المؤمنينَ لعلمائهم في الفروع (1) القبلة ؛ لأن الجهل بالصفات ليس جهلاً بالموصوفات ، وقال : « اختلفنا عبارة والمشار إليه واحد ) إلى أن قال : ( قال الإمام : ومعظم الأصحاب على ترك التكفير ، وقالوا : إنما نكفّر من جهل وجود الرب ، أو علم وجوده ولكن الله فعل فعلاً أو قال قولاً أجمعت الأمة على أنه لا يصدر ذلك إلا عن كافر » ) (۱) والفقهاء اليوم الذين يجوز تقليدهم ، والتمذهب بمذاهبهم .. هم أعلام المذاهب الأربعة المتبوعة ؛ أبو حنيفة ومالك والشافعي وأحمد ، رضي عنهم أجمعين، وأتباعهم اليوم من يمثل سواد المسلمين ، قال العلامة الدهلوي في « عقد الجيد في أحكام الاجتهاد والتقليد » ( ص ١٣ ) : ( قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «اتبعوا السواد الأعظم » ، ولما اندرست المذاهب الحقة إلا هذه الأربعة .. كان اتباعها اتباعاً للسواد الأعظم والخروج عنها خروجاً عن السواد الأعظم ) . ، وقال العلامة الصاوي في حاشيته على الجلالين ) ( ٢/ ٣٦٤ ) : ( ولا يجوز تقليد ما عدا المذاهب الأربعة ، ولو وافق قول الصحابة والحديث الصحيح والآية ، فالخارج عن المذاهب الأربعة ضال مضل ) وقال الإمام عبد القاهر البغدادي في «الفرق بين الفرق » ( ص ٢٦٧ ) : ) والصنف الثاني من أهل السنة والجماعة : أئمة الفقه من فريقي الرأي والحديث ؛ من الذين اعتقدوا مذاهب الصفاتية في الله تعالى وفي صفاته الأزلية ، وتبرَّؤوا من القدر والاعتزال، وأثبتوا رؤية الله تعالى بالأبصار ، من غير تشبيه ولا تعطيل ، ويدخل في هذه الجماعة : أصحاب مالك والشافعي والأوزاعي والثوري وأبي حنيفة وابن أبي ليلى ، وأصحاب أبي ثور ، وأصحاب أحمد بن حنبل ، وأهل الظاهر ، وسائر الفقهاء الذين اعتقدوا في الأبواب العقدية أصول الصفاتية ، ولم يخلطوا فقههم بشيء من بدع أهل الأهواء الضالة ) ، نعم ؛ لا يكون التقليد كمالاً، ولكنَّه هداية أقرتها الشريعة

Support is provided by al-Dahlawi, who cites the hadith 'Follow the greater mass' and notes that only these four madhabs remain, so following them is following the greater mass. Al-Sawi asserts that leaving these four is misguidance. Al-Baghdadi includes the imams of these madhabs in the second category of Ahl al-Sunna, praising their creedal orthodoxy. The passage concludes by affirming that taqlid is not perfection but is a guidance approved by the Shari‘a.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
الصفاتية
تقليد
تشبيه
تعطيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only the four madhabs are considered Ahl al-Sunna; other early jurists are not.
Correction: Al-Baghdadi includes many other scholars like al-Awza‘i, al-Thawri, and Ibn Abi Layla as part of Ahl al-Sunna, showing broader inclusivity.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about taqlid in the final sentence?
A) It is the highest level of religious practice.
B) It is not perfection but is a guidance approved by the Shari‘a.
C) It is prohibited.
D) It is only for laypeople.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is valid and divinely sanctioned, and the four madhabs are part of the broader Ahl al-Sunna tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Baghdadi lists scholars who united correct fiqh with correct creed. Is your own practice of Islam consistent in both areas, or do you separate them? Examine your heart: is there an area where you follow your desires rather than the Sifatiyya creed?
?
The passage says taqlid is not perfection but is guidance. In what specific area of your faith are you settling for the minimum when you are capable of striving for more understanding? What concrete step will you take this week to move closer to ijtihad in that matter?

Taqlid in Usul al-Din: Is It Sufficient?
Explains the ruling on taqlid in usul al-din with a condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling on taqlid in usul al-din according to many investigators, and the conditions under which it is considered sufficient.

Core Idea
Taqlid in creed is acceptable when based on firm resolve, especially when proofs are hard to grasp.

This passage addresses a key debate in Islamic theology: can a layperson simply follow the scholars in matters of faith without understanding the proofs? Sanusi presents the view of many investigators that it is sufficient if the believer is firmly resolved upon the truth, particularly when understanding the proofs is difficult.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the structure: first a question, then a response from the investigators.
Pay attention to the term 'tasmin' (firm resolve).
2
Identify key terms

Taqlid here means following a scholar without independent investigation.
3
Understand the condition
The investigators say taqlid is sufficient if the follower has 'tasmin' upon the truth. This is not blind imitation but a committed acceptance.
The condition is especially for those who find proofs difficult.

The Cause and Consequence of Compounded Ignorance
Sanusi explains the cause and punishment of compounded ignorance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the cause of compounded ignorance as explained by Sanusi, and how it leads to deprivation of divine guidance.

Core Idea
Pride in one's reasoning can cut off divine guidance.

Sanusi now delves into a critical psychological and spiritual pitfall: compounded ignorance. He explains how a person can become trapped in false certainty by trusting non-demonstrative proofs and feeling pride when they happen to be correct. This lesson reveals the root cause and the severe consequence – being deprived of further guidance from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very precise cause-effect structure.
2
Identify the cause of compounded ignorance
The passage states the cause clearly: the soul's confidence in non-demonstrative proofs and pride in its own reasoning when it hits the truth once.
Key phrase: 'وثوق النفس في العقليات بما ليس برهانيا'
3
Recognise the punishment
Sanusi then explains that the punishment for this arrogance is deprivation of guidance (عدم التسديد) in all other reflections, quoting Quran 7:146 to reinforce the point.
The punishment is directly linked to ungratefulness for the blessing of being correct.
4
Reflect on the scope
Note that compounded ignorance occurs in both rational and religious matters, and affects both independent seekers and blind followers.
This shows the universal nature of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسبب الجهل المركب : وثوق النفس في العقليات بما ليس برهانيا من الأدلة ، وتحسين الظن بما يستبد به من أنظارها واستنباطها لا سيما عندما تظهر لها الإصابة للحق في بعض أنظارها ، فتزهو وتعجب حينئذ ، وتقيس سائر أنظارها على ذلك النظر الذي من المولى الكريم تبارك وتعالى فيه بالتوفيق لدرك الحق ، فضلا منه جل وعلا. فعوقب هذا الناظر بالحرمان وعدم التسديد في سائر الأنظار ؛ لتكبره ، وإهماله شكر نعمة درك الصواب التي انفرد بإسدائها المولى جل وعلا ، وليس للعقل ولا للفكرة ولا للدليل الصحيح مادة وتركيبا فيه تأثير ألبتة ؛ لا بطريق التولد ، ولا بطريق التعليل ، وإهماله لزوم التواضع والفقر إلى المولى الكريم جل وعلا في كل نظر يقف بباله. قال الله عز وجل : ﴿ سَأَصْرِفُ عَنْ ءَايَتِيَ الَّذِينَ يَتَكَبَرُونَ فِي الْأَرْضِ بِغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٤٦]. ويكون أيضا هذا الجهل المركب في الشرعيات كما يكون في العقليات، ويكون من المقلدين كما يكون من الناظرين.
And the cause of compounded ignorance is: the soul's confidence in intellectual matters in what is not demonstrative among evidences, and thinking well of what it independently arrives at through its reflections and deductions, especially when it appears to have hit the truth in some of its reflections, so it exults and is amazed then, and it analogizes all its other reflections to that reflection in which the Generous Lord, Blessed and Exalted, granted success in attaining the truth, as a favor from Him, Mighty and Majestic. So this seeker is punished with deprivation and lack of guidance in all other reflections; due to his arrogance, and his neglect of thanking for the blessing of hitting the mark which the Lord, Mighty and Majestic, alone bestowed, and the intellect, the thought, and the sound proof, in material and composition, have absolutely no effect in it; neither by way of generation nor by way of causation, and his neglect of the necessity of humility and neediness toward the Generous Lord, Mighty and Majestic, in every reflection that occurs to his mind. Allah Almighty said: "I will turn away from My signs those who are arrogant in the land without right." And this compounded ignorance also occurs in religious matters as it occurs in intellectual matters, and it occurs among blind followers as it occurs among independent seekers.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the cause of compounded ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab) and its consequence. The author first identifies the cause: the soul's confidence in non-demonstrative proofs in rational matters, and thinking well of its own independent reasoning, especially when it happens to be correct once, leading to pride and measuring all other reasoning by that one success—attributing the success to itself rather than to God's favor. This arrogance results in punishment: deprivation of guidance in all other reflections, because the seeker fails to thank God for the blessing of hitting the mark, and imagines that the intellect, thought, or proof has some independent effect (by generation or causation), whereas in reality God alone grants success. The seeker also neglects humility and dependence on God in every reflection. The author then quotes Quran 7:146 to illustrate that God turns away the arrogant from understanding His signs. Finally, the author notes that this compounded ignorance occurs not only in rational matters but also in religious matters, and affects both independent seekers and blind followers.

Key Terms
جهل مركب
وثوق النفس
تسديد
تولد
تعليل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Confidence in one's intellectual success is always a virtue and a sign of sound reasoning.
Correction: Sanusi warns that such confidence, especially when based on non-demonstrative proofs, can lead to compounded ignorance and deprivation of divine guidance. True guidance comes from humility and recognizing Allah's favor.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the primary cause of compounded ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab)?
A) Lack of evidence in intellectual matters
B) The soul's confidence in non-demonstrative proofs and pride in its own reasoning
C) Blindly following scholars without questioning
D) Ignoring the Quran and Sunnah entirely

Key Takeaway
The root of compounded ignorance is pride in one's reasoning, which causes Allah to withhold guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Could that certainty have been a warning sign of compounded ignorance? What practical step will you take to stay dependent on Allah's guidance in every matter you study?

The Danger of Literalism in Matters of Faith
Sanusi warns that clinging to apparent meanings without distinguishing impossibility leads to kufr or bid'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why clinging to the apparent meanings of the Quran and Sunnah without rational distinction can lead to disbelief or innovation.

Core Idea
Literalism without rational discernment is a root of kufr or bid'ah.

Sanusi continues his enumeration of causes of error by warning against a dangerous approach: taking the apparent meanings of scripture without asking whether they imply something impossible. This lesson explains why this is not just a methodological mistake but a foundation for serious theological deviation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Sanusi presents the sixth cause in a concise, forceful manner.
2
Understand key terms
Focus on the terms 'zawahir' (apparent meanings) and 'mustahil' (impossible). Understand that 'zawahir' are not rejected outright, but must be evaluated for rational possibility.
3
Grasp the gravity of the ruling
Sanusi calls this approach 'asl al-kufr aw al-bid'a' — a root of disbelief or innovation. This is a very strong condemnation, indicating that the error is not minor.
4
Consider examples
Think of anthropomorphic verses (e.g., 'the hand of Allah') — if taken literally, they imply physicality, which is impossible for God. This is the type of situation Sanusi warns about.
5
Reflect on the solution
When the apparent meaning leads to impossibility, the correct approach is ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation) or tafwid (consigning the meaning to God). This preserves faith while respecting reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأمر السادس؛ وهو التمسك في عقائد الإيمان بمجرد ظواهر الكتاب والسنة من غير تفصيل بين ما يستحيل ظاهرها وما لا يستحيل: فلا خفاء في كونه أصلا للكفر أو البدعة
And as for the sixth matter—namely, clinging in the beliefs of faith to mere apparent meanings of the Book and the Sunna, without distinguishing between what has an impossible apparent meaning and what does not: there is no concealment in it being a root of disbelief or innovation.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage identifies the sixth cause of error in matters of faith: clinging to the literal or apparent meanings (zawahir) of the Quran and Sunnah without distinguishing between what is rationally impossible in its apparent sense and what is not. Sanusi declares that this approach is clearly a root (asl) of either kufr (disbelief) or bid'ah (heretical innovation). The implication is that when an apparent meaning leads to something rationally impossible (mustahil), such as anthropomorphism, it must be interpreted metaphorically (ta'wil) or consigned to God (tafwid). Failure to do so results in theological error.

Key Terms
ظواهر الكتاب والسنة
أصل الكفر
بدعة
يستحيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think any apparent meaning of Quran or Sunnah must be taken literally, no matter what.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly warns that this approach, without distinguishing impossibility, is a root of disbelief or innovation. When the apparent meaning implies something impossible for God, it must be interpreted allegorically.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the ruling on clinging to the apparent meanings of the Quran and Sunnah in matters of faith without distinguishing between possible and impossible?
A) It is recommended as a sign of piety
B) It is a root of disbelief or innovation
C) It is permissible as long as one follows a madhhab
D) It is obligatory to take everything literally

Key Takeaway
Clinging to apparent meanings without rational discernment is a root of disbelief or innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Core Idea
Compound ignorance can strike anyone, whether rational investigator or blind follower.

This short but significant passage broadens our understanding of compound ignorance. The author asserts that this error is not confined to those who reason rationally; it also affects religious matters and even those who simply follow tradition without investigation.

The Sixth Error: Clinging to Apparent Meanings Without Reason
Sanusi defines the sixth error and illustrates it with the dualist misinterpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why relying solely on the apparent meanings of scripture without considering rational impossibility can lead to unbelief or innovation.

Core Idea
Apparent meanings of scripture must be filtered through rational impossibility.

Imam Sanusi continues his list of errors by warning against a dangerous method: taking the literal, apparent meanings of the Quran and Sunnah without checking whether those meanings are rationally impossible. He declares this approach a root of either kufr or bid‘a. To illustrate, he recounts how the dualists misinterpreted a verse about light, leading them to shirk.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation. Notice how Sanusi defines the error and then gives an example.
The passage uses a specific term 'استحالة' (impossibility) which is key.
2
Identify the error and its consequence
Find where Sanusi states that this error is a 'root of kufr or bid'a'. Reflect on why this is so serious.
The error is not in using scripture, but in using it without rational discernment.
3
Analyze the dualist example
Examine how the dualists misinterpreted the verse 'Allah is the light of the heavens and the earth'. Why did their interpretation lead to kufr?
They ignored the rational impossibility of light being divine because light is changeable and contingent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأمر السادس؛ وهو التمسُّكُ في عقائدِ الإيمان بمجرَّدِ ظواهر الكتاب والسنَّةِ مِنْ غيرِ تفصيل بين ما يستحيل ظاهرُه منها وما لا يستحيلُ : فلا خفاء في كونه أصلاً للكفر أو البدعة. أمَّا الكفرُ : فكأخذ الثنويَّةِ القائلين بألوهِيَّةِ النور والظلمةِ مِنْ قولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ اللَّهُ نُورُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ﴾ : أنَّ النور أحدُ الإلهين واسمُهُ : الله ، ولم ينظروا إلى استحالة كون النورِ إلهاً ؛ لأنَّه متغير حادث ، يوجد وينعدم ، والإله يستحيل عليه التغيرُ ، ويجب له القدم والبقاء
And as for the sixth matter: it is clinging in the beliefs of faith to mere apparent meanings of the Book and the Sunna without distinguishing between that whose apparent meaning is impossible and that whose apparent meaning is not impossible. There is no concealment that it is a root of unbelief or innovation. As for unbelief: such as the dualists who assert the divinity of light and darkness taking from His statement (the Lord of might): 'Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth' that light is one of the two gods and its name is Allah, and they did not consider the impossibility of light being a god; because it is changeable, contingent, it exists and ceases, while the divine is impossible for change, and pre-eternity and everlastingness are necessary for Him.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage identifies the sixth error in matters of creed: relying solely on the apparent meanings of scripture without considering whether those apparent meanings are rationally impossible. It declares this error to be a root (aṣl) of either unbelief (kufr) or innovation (bid‘a). The author then provides a concrete example of kufr: the dualists (al-thunawiyya) who misinterpreted the verse 'Allah is the Light of the heavens and the earth' to claim that light is one of two gods, called 'Allah'. They failed to recognise the impossibility of light being divine because light is changeable and contingent, whereas God must be unchanging and pre-eternal. The example illustrates how ignoring rational impossibility in scriptural interpretation leads directly to kufr.

Two Valid Methods for Interpreting Impossible Apparent Meanings
Author explains tafwid (salaf) and ta'wil (khalaf) as responses to impossible apparent meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two legitimate methodologies—tafwid (delegation) and ta'wil (interpretation)—that scholars use to resolve apparent conflicts between scripture and reason.

Core Idea
Both tafwid and ta'wil are valid; the difference lies in specifying a meaning.

When the apparent meaning of a Quranic verse or hadith seems to contradict rational truths, scholars do not reject the text. Instead, they employ either tafwid (delegating the true meaning to Allah) or ta'wil (assigning a linguistically valid, reason-compatible meaning). The following passage from Sanusi introduces these two approaches, citing the Salaf for tafwid and Imam al-Haramayn for ta'wil, and gives an example of ta'wil for the verse about Allah being 'light.'

Guided Path
1
Read the passage in Arabic and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the two main options: tafwid and ta'wil.
The passage is dense; take your time to see the structure.
2
Identify the two methods
Find where the text describes the first method (tafwid) and the second method (ta'wil). Note who is associated with each.
The Salaf are linked to tafwid; Imam al-Haramayn and many imams to ta'wil.
3
Understand the example of ta'wil
The passage gives a sample ta'wil for the 'light' verse. See how metaphor (isti'ara) and simile (tashbih baligh) are used to reconcile the apparent meaning with reason.
The example shows that 'light' can mean guidance and 'darkness' non-existence.
4
Reflect on why both methods are valid
Consider that both approaches respect the divine origin of the text while preserving rational consistency. Think about why a scholar might choose one over the other.
This connects to the broader principle of avoiding anthropomorphism (tashbih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان كذلك وجبَ حمل الآية على خلاف ظاهرها: إما مع التفويض إلى المولى تبارك وتعالى في تعيين المراد منها؛ وهو مذهب السلف في جنس هذه الظواهر وإما مع تعيين معنى يصح إرادته بهذا اللفظ في لغة العرب؛ لأنَّ القرآنَ نزلَ بألسنتهم، وهو مذهبُ إمام الحرمين وكثيرٍ مِنَ الأئمَّةِ. ولهم في ذلك تأويلات مذكورةٌ في كتب التفسير، من جملتها: أَنَّهُ يحتمل أنْ يكونَ اللفظ خرجَ مخرج الاستعارة، أو التشبيه البليغ؛ بأنْ جُعِلَ العدمُ كظلمة استتر فيه وجود الكائناتِ
And if that is the case, it is necessary to interpret the verse contrary to its apparent meaning: either with delegation to the Lord, Blessed and Exalted, in specifying the intended meaning – and this is the way of the Salaf concerning such apparent texts – or by specifying a meaning that can be intended by this word in the Arabic language, because the Qur'an was revealed in their tongues, and this is the way of Imam al-Haramayn and many of the imams. And they have regarding that interpretations mentioned in the books of tafsir, among them: that the wording may have come out as metaphor or beautiful simile, such that non-existence is made as a veil in which the existence of beings is hidden.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents the two legitimate methodologies for dealing with scriptural texts whose apparent meaning is rationally impossible. The first is tafwid (delegation): leaving the true meaning to Allah without specifying it; this is attributed to the Salaf (early Muslims). The second is ta'wil (interpretation): assigning a linguistically valid meaning that is consistent with reason; this is attributed to Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) and many later imams. The passage then gives an example of such interpretations for the 'light' verse: the wording might be metaphorical or a beautiful simile, explaining that 'light' refers to guidance and 'darkness' refers to non-existence, meaning that Allah's guidance illuminates the existence of things from non-existence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tafwid and ta'wil are opposed and only one is correct.
Correction: The passage presents both as valid approaches for different groups: tafwid for the Salaf, ta'wil for Imam al-Haramayn and many imams. Both are legitimate methods to uphold divine transcendence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two methods are valid for dealing with verses whose apparent meaning is impossible?

B) Tafwid (delegation) and ta'wil (interpretation)
C) Literalism and allegory
D) Silence and denial

Key Takeaway
When scripture appears to conflict with reason, scholars either delegate the true meaning to Allah (tafwid) or interpret it in a linguistically sound way (ta'wil), both preserving divine transcendence.

?

Be honest: what does that reveal about your trust in Allah's words versus your need for rational clarity?
?

Or do you truly rest in reliance on Allah, even when your mind is unsatisfied? Tonight, sit with one such verse and let the uncertainty drive you to deeper humility in your prayer.
?

Are you willing to set aside a comfortable interpretation if it is not grounded in the linguistic usage the Qur'an came with? Answer to yourself, not to this question.

The General Rule for Problematic Texts with One Interpretation
Sanusi states the general rule for problematic texts with only one possible interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general rule that Sanusi applies to problematic texts in the Qur'an and Sunnah when only one interpretation is rationally possible.

Core Idea
When a text can only mean one thing, you must take it.

Sanusi provides a clear methodological principle for interpreting scriptural passages that seem to attribute impossible qualities to Allah. The rule is straightforward: if the apparent meaning is impossible and there is only one valid interpretation, that interpretation must be adopted. This lesson explains the rule and walks through the famous example of the verse 'He is with you wherever you are.'

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let Sanusi's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how the author first notes the abundance of such texts, then gives the rule, then provides an example.
2
Identify the rule and its condition
Find the precise wording of the rule: 'if it does not accept from ta'wil except one meaning, then it must be taken upon it.' Note that the condition is that the apparent meaning is impossible and only one ta'wil is possible.
This is a conditional statement: condition + consequence.
3
Examine the example
See how the verse 'He is with you' is analyzed. The apparent meaning (spatial nearness) is impossible because it is an attribute of bodies. The only possible interpretation is 'encompassing in knowledge, hearing, and sight' as indicated by the context.
This example illustrates both the impossibility and the single possible meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومشكلاتُ الكتاب والسنَّةِ كثيرةٌ جداً ، وقد صنف العلماء جمعها والكلام عليها تصانيف (۲) ، والضابط الجُمْلِيُّ في جميعها : أَنَّ كل مشكل منها مستحيل الظاهر فإنَّهُ يُنظَرُ فيهِ : فإنْ كانَ لا يقبلُ مِنَ التأويل إلا معنى واحداً.. وجبَ أَنْ يُحمَلَ عليه ؛ كقوله تعالى : ﴿ وَهُوَ مَعَكُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ ﴾ [الحديد : ٤] ، فإِنَّ المعيَّة بالتحيز والحلول في المكان مستحيلة على المولى تبارك وتعالى ؛ لأَنَّهَا مِنْ صفاتِ الأجسامِ ، فتعيَّنَ صرفُ الكلام عن ظاهرِه ، ولا يقبلُ هنا إلا تأويلاً واحداً دل عليه السياقُ ؛ وهو المعيَّةُ بالإحاطة علماً وسمعاً وبصراً (٣) .
And the problems of the Book and the Sunnah are very many, and the scholars have authored works collecting them and discussing them. The general rule regarding all of them: that every problematic text whose apparent meaning is impossible, then it is looked into: if it does not accept from ta'wil except one meaning, then it must be taken upon it; like His statement, the Most High: "And He is with you wherever you are" [al-Hadid: 4]. For verily, 'being with' in the sense of occupying space and indwelling in a place is impossible for the Lord, Blessed and Most High, because it is from the attributes of bodies. So it is determined to divert the speech from its apparent meaning, and it does not accept here except one ta'wil indicated by the context: which is 'being with' in the sense of encompassing in knowledge, hearing, and sight.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage provides the general principle (ضابط جملّي) for interpreting problematic texts in the Qur'an and Sunnah. The author first notes that such texts are abundant and scholars have compiled works on them. He then states the rule: for every problematic text whose apparent meaning is impossible (for Allah), we examine it. If it only accepts one possible interpretation (ta'wil), then we must adopt it. He gives the example of the verse 'He is with you wherever you are.' The apparent meaning of spatial nearness is impossible because it is a bodily attribute. Therefore, the only possible interpretation is that of encompassing knowledge, hearing, and sight, as indicated by the context.

Key Terms
مشكلات
تأويل
المعية
التحيز
الحلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that any ambiguous text must be interpreted metaphorically, regardless of how many interpretations are possible.
Correction: The author specifies that the rule applies only when exactly one interpretation is possible. If multiple interpretations are possible, different rules may apply. The example shows that the single possible interpretation must be adopted.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rule for a problematic verse that has only one possible interpretation (ta'wil)?
A) It must be left as it is without interpretation.
B) It must be taken upon that interpretation.
C) It must be interpreted in multiple ways.
D) It must be rejected.

Key Takeaway
The general rule: if a problematic text has only one possible interpretation, it must be adopted, as with the verse 'He is with you' meaning encompassing knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are there any other verses about Allah's attributes (like 'the Most Merciful established Himself above the Throne') that you find confusing? Will you now commit to learning the correct ta'wil from scholars rather than settling for a literal, physical meaning?
